    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer2108457889968031979">How much of an impact can an animal have? How many lives can one cat touch? How is it possible for an abandoned kitten to transform a small library, save a classic American town, and eventually become famous around the world? You can't even begin to answer those questions until you hear the charming story of Dewey Readmore Books, the beloved library cat of Spencer, Iowa.<br/><br/>De</span>
  <span id="freeText2108457889968031979" style="display:none">How much of an impact can an animal have? How many lives can one cat touch? How is it possible for an abandoned kitten to transform a small library, save a classic American town, and eventually become famous around the world? You can't even begin to answer those questions until you hear the charming story of Dewey Readmore Books, the beloved library cat of Spencer, Iowa.<br /><br />Dewey's story starts in the worst possible way. Only a few weeks old, on the coldest night of the year, he was stuffed into the returned book slot at the Spencer Public Library. He was found the next working by library director Vicki Myron, a single mother who had survived the loss of her family farm, a breast cancer scare, and an alcoholic husband. Dewey won her heart, and the hearts of the staff, by pulling himself up and hobbling on frostbitten feet to nudge each of hem in a gesture of thanks and love. For the next nineteen years, he never stopped charming the people of Spencer with this enthusiasm, warmth, humility (for a cat), and, above all, his sixth sense about who needed him most.<br /><br />As his fame grew from town to town, then state to state, and finally, amazingly, worldwide, Dewey became more than just a friend; he became a source of pride for an extraordinary Heartland farming town pulling its way slowly back from the greatest crisis in its long history.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Yes, it is. Myron does a amazing job of portraying her life and the lives of her customers. Also, the way she describes Dewey and his personality is a<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Yes, it is. Myron does a amazing job of portraying her life and the lives of her customers. Also, the way she describes Dewey and his personality is adorable. If you like cat books, depressing back story's, and small town America, than you will probably find this little gem of a book very interesting. I know I did.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I just finished the book and Dewey lives a full life until he is 18. At the age of 18, Vicki gets called back into work because Dewey is acting strang<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I just finished the book and Dewey lives a full life until he is 18. At the age of 18, Vicki gets called back into work because Dewey is acting strangely. Vicki takes him to the vet, where they discover a tumor in his stomach. His death was very peaceful. This happens in Chapter 26. <br /><br />I understand your comment. The novel is very good- a remarkable cat that touches the lives of many. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6860539709194428514">Wow, am I in the minority with this one. I like cats, I like libraries, and I've even known a library cat or two. I didn't expect to rave about this book quite as much as many others have done, but I also didn't expect to think so very little of it. <br/><br/>A few cute anecdotes notwithstanding, there is just nothing special about this book.   <span id="freeText6860539709194428514" style="display:none">Wow, am I in the minority with this one. I like cats, I like libraries, and I've even known a library cat or two. I didn't expect to rave about this book quite as much as many others have done, but I also didn't expect to think so very little of it. <br /><br />A few cute anecdotes notwithstanding, there is just nothing special about this book. Any pet owner could write as much (and many would do it markedly better). The tone of the author was grating to me, and her experiences were not nearly as interesting as she seemed to think they were. At its core, this is a not uncommon tale with startlingly inflated publicity.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82156882?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kinga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kinga" href="/user/show/110812-kinga">Kinga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/110812-kinga?shelf=pub-2008">pub-2008</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82156882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12442470979301358655">I didn't expect this book to be quality literature and of course it wasn't. It was a feel-good book, only I've noticed that most feel-good books actually make me feel nauseous instead of good. Especially those that idealize small town America.<br/><br/>I thought I was going to scream if I had to read another paragraph about how amazing the town of Spencer, Iowa is. To give you a taste:<br/>"That's another of Spencer's unique and valuable assets: its people. We are good, solid, hardworking midwesterners. We are</span>
  <span id="freeText12442470979301358655" style="display:none">I didn't expect this book to be quality literature and of course it wasn't. It was a feel-good book, only I've noticed that most feel-good books actually make me feel nauseous instead of good. Especially those that idealize small town America.<br /><br />I thought I was going to scream if I had to read another paragraph about how amazing the town of Spencer, Iowa is. To give you a taste:<br />"That's another of Spencer's unique and valuable assets: its people. We are good, solid, hardworking midwesterners. We are proud but humble. We don't brag."<br />Sure they don't. I have just read a 275 page long eulogy to Spencer and its people.<br /><br />Try as she might Vicki Myron didn't fool me. Under a heavy sugar coat I could see rotten flesh bubbling with old grudges, grievances and hostilities. I would love to read more about that but I guess it was a no go as the people's real names were used.<br /><br />The book was really chopped (a bit like my review). There were parts about Dewey, bits about Vicky's life, and the history of the town all thrown in together. They didn't blend very well but I was slightly entertained by some chapters so I am giving it two stars.<br />Oh yeah, the cat was cute.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmaletta Hilton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmaletta Hilton" href="/user/show/950738-carmaletta-hilton">Carmaletta Hilton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45763888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7505516937483017611">I thought I was reading a book about a cat, but I wound up reading a book about a woman with a lot of troubles in her life. For every chapter that was actually about Dewey, there seemed to be 2 or 3 that were just about her. I'm very sorry for the losses in this woman's life, and the things she went through, but that's not what I set out to read. I expected a good, light-hearted story about a cat, but every time I reached a point where my spirits were lifted, Ms. Myron brought it all crashing do</span>
  <span id="freeText7505516937483017611" style="display:none">I thought I was reading a book about a cat, but I wound up reading a book about a woman with a lot of troubles in her life. For every chapter that was actually about Dewey, there seemed to be 2 or 3 that were just about her. I'm very sorry for the losses in this woman's life, and the things she went through, but that's not what I set out to read. I expected a good, light-hearted story about a cat, but every time I reached a point where my spirits were lifted, Ms. Myron brought it all crashing down with the next crisis/drama involving herself and her family. <br /><br />There were some very sweet stories about the cat, which pushes it from one star to two. I wish there had been more. I also think it would have been a good idea to include actual testimony about Dewey from people he had touched. Also, some of the articles written about Dewey could have been included instead of the little "notes" recreated. They may have been cute, but honestly, by the time the longer ones were put in there, I wasn't even reading them.<br /><br />Yet another book that I had to force myself to finish.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1162636633" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1162636633" />
    <a title="Bionic Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean"><img alt="Bionic Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586709362p2/19300421.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1162636633?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bionic Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bionic Jean" href="/user/show/19300421-bionic-jean">Bionic Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8141643-dewey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=read-authors-m-p">read-authors-m-p</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19300421-bionic-jean?shelf=read-authors-u-z">read-authors-u-z</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162636633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7043935253636766876">There is a common idiomatic phrase, <i>"it does exactly what it says on the tin"</i>. Well in the case of <b>Dewey: The small-town library-cat who touched the world</b> by Vicki Myron and Bret Witter, it doesn't. The book is a bit of a hotch-potch. <br/><br/>It starts out as a very promising and touching animal story. The librarian of a small town library in Spencer, Iowa, discovers a tiny, frozen, furry bundle in the drop-box of her library. Incredibly, the bundle proves to be a kitten who is still alive, though barel</span>
  <span id="freeText7043935253636766876" style="display:none">There is a common idiomatic phrase, <i>"it does exactly what it says on the tin"</i>. Well in the case of <b>Dewey: The small-town library-cat who touched the world</b> by Vicki Myron and Bret Witter, it doesn't. The book is a bit of a hotch-potch. <br /><br />It starts out as a very promising and touching animal story. The librarian of a small town library in Spencer, Iowa, discovers a tiny, frozen, furry bundle in the drop-box of her library. Incredibly, the bundle proves to be a kitten who is still alive, though barely. Which animal-lover could not fail to be moved by such an opening - especially knowing that it was a true story? The next few chapters describe how the kitten wins everyone's hearts, both staff and public. Sometimes the events are moving, sometimes comical, just as all encounters with domestic animals are in real life. Eventually the long-haired ginger kitten becomes formally adopted as a library cat, and named <i>"Dewey</i> (after the library system) <i>Readmore Books"</i>.<br /><br />A charming story. I was looking forward to the rest. Then quite a lot about the town, Spencer,'s history started to intrude. Fair enough though; it put everything in context. Spencer had had a chequered past, with changing farming and industrial needs, the Depression, the recession. Various new developments had been proposed. As a reader I went along with it, wondering when I could chuckle at Dewey's antics again. Chapter 5 was entitled, <i>"Catnip and rubber bands"</i>. Ah yes! I knew about those. I settled down happily. <br /><br />Gradually it shifted focus. From the introduction we had learnt a little about Spencer and the state of Iowa. This was useful information, especially for non-American readers. And the book says that even Americans tend to think of Iowa as a <i>"place you fly over on your way to somewhere else."</i> Iowa is predominantly devoted to the farming industry; growing corn, and manufacturing all the by-products of corn, such as corn starch, xanthan gum, ethanol etc. All the additives which 21st century life seems to need. Apparently a startling 70 per cent of the average American diet is corn, in one form or another. <br /><br />But then in addition to all the history, the shift of emphasis to facts and figures about trade and industry, we also begin to get autobiographical information about Vicki Myron; her ancestors, her friends and co-workers, the bigwigs in the town, her current family. So now we have three different components. Searching for bits about the cat Dewey began to feel like searching for gold within the corn of Iowa.<br /><br />Vicki Myron's family certainly had a rough life. They seemed to have more than their fair share of bad luck and poverty, illnesses such as cancer and depression, and alcoholism and suicide. Vicki Myron herself had a troubled marriage, had to fight for the right to have a professional job, to bring up her daughter on her own, to cope with teenage alienation, and to deal with her own chronic ill-health. Many of Spencer's inhabitants suffered, some in similar ways. Life was hard, and continues to be so for many small-town folk. <br /><br />It would be wrong to lessen in any way the courage shown by these individuals, who have to work so hard to survive, and to continue in their community's way of life. The "message" of the book is that Dewey helped. Because they began to care about him, people began to regain their self-respect when they lost their jobs, or when times were tough and the future looked bleak. They began to smile more, and to fight to survive. There are stories about disabled children, or children who would never speak - until they met Dewey. Dewey brought people together, and made the library a focus for the community. And there are stories of visiting families from all over the world, as the fame of this little cat grew, of articles published in magazines, and even a small slot in a Japanese film.<br /><br />I have no doubt this is true. Animals have a remarkable facility to make humans feel better. Stroking a pet has been shown to lessen stress, and slow down the heart rate. But the blurb of the book says,<br /><br /><i>"This is the heart-warming and unforgettable story of a truly idiosyncratic cat with a strong sense of loyalty and love, and a taste for fast-food"</i>.<br /><br />There is just too much history of Iowa, too much ethnography, and far too much biography and autobiography, however admirable these people are. Perhaps it would interest some readers in itself, but it is of only limited interest in a book supposedly about a cat.<br /><br />The book really needed to decide its focus from the beginning, and state it honestly. The idea came from Vicki Myron, but it was either ghost-written or developed into a full-length book by Bret Witter. It feels very much as though it was artificially expanded. On his writer's page Bret Witter describes himself as,<br /><br /><i>"a full-time professional writer who specializes in contemporary nonfiction, usually working with a co-author to tell their inspiring true story"</i><br /><br />which also goes a long way to explain the occasional lapses into sentimental schmaltz, such as,<br /><br /><i>"Is that what Iowa is all about? Maybe the heartland isn't just the place in the middle of the country; maybe it's also the place in the middle of your chest."</i><br /><br />Unfortunately there's quite a lot of that tweeness. Pure corn. (With apologies to Iowa's farming industry for the pun.)<br /><br />This reader has a sneaky suspicion that the "saviour" side of Dewey is overly stressed to fit the role he is cast in to save this small town and its people. I've no doubt he was popular, and all cats have their unique special abilities, but <i>"touched the world"</i>? There are sequels too, which is probably primarily a business decision. The material here about Dewey would have been better presented as a short book - and been far more entertaining too.<br /><br />My local library also has a cat. I almost fell over him one morning when I went through the main door; he was lapping at a saucer of milk. Sometimes I find him asleep in the children's section, next to the radiator. He's also a ginger cat, similar to Dewey. This book is worth buying for the cover alone, which has a beautiful picture of Dewey in his prime. I love cats, and reading about animals, providing the book is not overly twee.<br /><br />But this book does not do what it says on the tin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7043935253636766876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_25460150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/25460150" />
    <a title="Tom Franklin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/661076-tom-franklin"><img alt="Tom Franklin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1207280002p2/661076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/25460150?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom Franklin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom Franklin" href="/user/show/661076-tom-franklin">Tom Franklin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer25460150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4874629864763735396">Vicky Myron's "Dewey" is a book about many things: life in small town Iowa, Vicky's own life history, the important role a library can play in the life and identity of a community and, of course, Dewey Readmore Books, one of the best known and well loved cats in the world.<br/><br/>Despite the variety of topics Myron writes about, her book holds together so well through her decision to write honestly about everything. Some of her personal and family history was obviously difficult to write about, but its </span>
  <span id="freeText4874629864763735396" style="display:none">Vicky Myron's "Dewey" is a book about many things: life in small town Iowa, Vicky's own life history, the important role a library can play in the life and identity of a community and, of course, Dewey Readmore Books, one of the best known and well loved cats in the world.<br /><br />Despite the variety of topics Myron writes about, her book holds together so well through her decision to write honestly about everything. Some of her personal and family history was obviously difficult to write about, but its her willingness to do so that makes this book much more than a simple book about a library cat.<br /><br />Dewey was, of course, the catalyst (<i>cat</i>alyst) for writing the book and his story is a great one. His adventures as a library cat make for entertaining reading and any cat lover will appreciate Dewey's spirit and personality. Even more, cat lovers will nod knowingly as they read about the strong emotional bond Dewey has with those closest to him.<br /><br />While Myron was Dewey's "mom", she also has the wisdom and the insight to understand the impact one special cat can have on individual lives as well as an entire community. She also does a fine job honoring and respecting that one special cat and the impact he had on her life.<br /><br />...</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_529411263" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529411263" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529411263?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=got-in-2013">got-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=nonfiction-i-stayed-awake-through">nonfiction-i-stayed-awake-through</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529411263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16643926190938055299"><b> “A great library doesn't have to be big or beautiful. It doesn't have to have the best facilities or the most efficient staff or the most users. A great library provides. It is enmeshed in the life of a community in a way that makes it indispensable. A great library is one nobody notices because it is always there, and always has what people need.” </b><br/><br/>A non-fiction book about an adorable cat and a small town's history. The cat helps change that history and give the town's heart a bit more beat. Un</span>
  <span id="freeText16643926190938055299" style="display:none"><b> “A great library doesn't have to be big or beautiful. It doesn't have to have the best facilities or the most efficient staff or the most users. A great library provides. It is enmeshed in the life of a community in a way that makes it indispensable. A great library is one nobody notices because it is always there, and always has what people need.” </b><br><br>A non-fiction book about an adorable cat and a small town's history. The cat helps change that history and give the town's heart a bit more beat. Until they acted like asses at the end of his life and started taking that for granted (typical people!) It really comes across as an almost miraculous story when the little bundle of kitten was discovered in the mail slot like discarded trash. I'm sure the librarians never imagined how popular the cat would eventually become and how much it would affect the life of the librarian, Vicki.<br><br>While some of the town lore was interesting, I admit to skimming some of it. The fun antics of Dewey captivated me - I'm a cat lover myself so could relate to some of the chilling spots, box obsessions and personality quirks, but there were new cat weirdness situations that was new to me. For example, Dewey LOVES rubber bands, so much so that they had to keep them under lock and key.						<br><br>The cat's adorable, and if you ever wanted to know how a cat would adapt to living in a library, here you go. Cats and books go together, right?		<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487212322i/21987902._SX540_.jpg" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg">				<br><br>It's not just a long book about staring at a cat, but how Dewey changed the lives of several with their own histories. When Dewey started becoming one of the furry famous, the stories of interviews and different cat food commercials were more interesting that you'd think judging off description alone. Sweet stories overload - There's a tragically handicapped girl who smiled for the first time in years with Dewey's attention, people not wanting to disturb the cards because Dewey was laying in the box, people coming across the country in family trips to find the legendary cat.						<br><br>Dewey' doesn't just dish out the sweet stuff, though - it talks about the naysayers, the political library committees (grrr), and of course how people were less accepting of the cat who had done so much for the town with revenue and aid when he gets older and less pleasingly fuzzy. <br><br>The ending is, of course, sad. I knew what was coming so that softened the blow, but I was surprised (and touched) with how much Vicki was affected for life. I won't spoil the ending with how she changes her life in a huge way, but it adds a sense of loyalty and charm to a book that was already unique and special.<br><br>Besides being a treat for cat lovers, it digs into the details of how special libraries are and how much they offer patrons, especially in small towns that struggle. Through economic woes, factory shut-downs, numerous changes, the librarian and Dewey stuck around to do what they could in the small amount of time life allotted them. After reading the stories of Dewey and all his little habits, Vicki's life and her struggles with her daughter and cancer, I came to really feel like I knew both of them in a way. That's one of the best things a non-fiction book can do for a person, be authentic enough to give that personal connection.						<br><br>Read it for the cat, read it for the memories of the small town in Iowa, read it for the library ambience - it's worth a look even if it's just for the adorable pictures that grace the chapter headings.						<br><br>												</span>
  <a data-text-id="16643926190938055299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_920560209" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920560209" />
    <a title="Ashley Marie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie"><img alt="Ashley Marie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471208025p2/29787548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920560209?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley Marie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley Marie " href="/user/show/29787548-ashley-marie">Ashley Marie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=might-have-cried">might-have-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=audiobook-would-recommend">audiobook-would-recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29787548-ashley-marie?shelf=nonfiction-history">nonfiction-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920560209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2256372413289684142">Firstly, thank you all for <s>enjoying</s> putting up with my cat-story updates. As pet lovers know, we all need to talk about our pets to random strangers from time to time, so that was rather therapeutic. <br/><br/>Dewey's story is an incredible one. And, as shown by the 20-year difference from the beginning to the end of the book, it's highly unlikely the library would have adopted a cat in this day and age. As Vicki notes, there were complaints after Dewey showed up and it was decided that he would stay, but</span>
  <span id="freeText2256372413289684142" style="display:none">Firstly, thank you all for <s>enjoying</s> putting up with my cat-story updates. As pet lovers know, we all need to talk about our pets to random strangers from time to time, so that was rather therapeutic. <br /><br />Dewey's story is an incredible one. And, as shown by the 20-year difference from the beginning to the end of the book, it's highly unlikely the library would have adopted a cat in this day and age. As Vicki notes, there were complaints after Dewey showed up and it was decided that he would stay, but they appeared to be few and far between. Nowadays it would probably be unheard of because of the sheer number of people with allergies and the like. But I'm glad for Dewey and the Spencer library; glad this was able to happen and that Dewey was able to help so many people in his way, as animals do. I'm not sure why, but cats and books have always seemed to go hand-in-hand to me (I've got a photo blog basically dedicated to it), and this story was so sweet.<br /><br />I really found myself relating to Vicki even when she went off on tangents about the town's history or her family; I grew up in a small town, and my corner of Ohio is often surrounded by cornfields as much as her spot in Iowa seems to be, once you get out of the city a little way. Vicki's library stories also make me so thankful for the little branch library I had available when I was in school; by the time I was in high school, the branch library had been relocated and plopped square between the middle school and high school buildings and was adjoined to them via the high school library, so if the school library didn't have something I could pop through the door to the branch and be right back to school again in a minute. Now, here in Akron, we have branches all over the place and several of those Little Free Library spots, but I'm enormously spoiled by the main library. I can just imagine trying to have a library cat there -- poor thing would probably get lost and we wouldn't see him for days! But Dewey seems to have been a perfect fit for that little library in Iowa.<br /><br />I really appreciated Vicki's voice in this book; she came through so clearly, aided no doubt by Susan McInerney's excellent narration in the audiobook. Reading this was like talking pets, books and life with a friend; casual, but to the point and expressive. Like my own pets (cats or otherwise), Dewey will always have a place in my heart, alongside Cleo, Lava and all the other wonderful animal stories out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2256372413289684142" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17529390945710591135">Ignore the "to-read" following "never-got-to-the-last-page." Only 210 more pages to go the distance and earn the right to give one star to DEWEY -- but I left the ring. Another ten pages -- and I might have been "down for the count" in Spencer, Iowa. Sorry -- kitty lovers. By the way, I'm one of you. Sorry -- Simple Simon lovers. And sorry -- small-town, out-in-the-middle-of-nowhere, lovers. This book may be for you, but it's not for me. <br/><br/>When I hated grading freshman compositions, but before the</span>
  <span id="freeText17529390945710591135" style="display:none">Ignore the "to-read" following "never-got-to-the-last-page." Only 210 more pages to go the distance and earn the right to give one star to DEWEY -- but I left the ring. Another ten pages -- and I might have been "down for the count" in Spencer, Iowa. Sorry -- kitty lovers. By the way, I'm one of you. Sorry -- Simple Simon lovers. And sorry -- small-town, out-in-the-middle-of-nowhere, lovers. This book may be for you, but it's not for me. <br /><br />When I hated grading freshman compositions, but before they started giving me chest pains (diagnosed as unexpressed anger), a friend showed me Richard Armour's "Lines Long After Pope, By a Reader of Freshman Themes." These few lines drove thirty-two years (not as long as a quick trip to Iowa seemed to take) from subconscious to conscious territory so that, by Chapter 7 of DEWEY, I could mumble: "Small wit is theirs,/ in shopworn phrases dressed,/ what oft was thought/ and twice as well expressed." <br /><br />I had been told that I would love DEWEY. Because I love cats??? I didn't need more reasons to believe that it's good to expect nothing and be grateful for anything acceptable, but I now have something else to confirm that belief. If, as Alexander Pope proposed, "True Wit is Nature to advantage dressed,/ What oft was thought, but ne'er so well expressed" ("An Essay on Criticism" II.297-98), Vicki Myron (with Bret Witter) deserves the Half-Wit Award for getting the part about dressing up Nature. With characters making comments such as "Where there's a will, there's a way"(45),though, you think, "Richard Armour, your freshmen graduated and went on to write DEWEY: THE SMALL-TOWN CAT WHO TOUCHED THE WORLD. Granted, I may have missed the best parts of this book; but until my cats stop sitting on books and decide to learn to read, I don't expect to find out if I have indeed ignored choice morsels in the litter box. <br /> </span>

How is it possible for an abandoned kitten to transform a small library, save a classic American town, and eventually become famous around the world? You can't even begin to answer those questions until you hear the charming story of Dewey Readmore Books, the beloved library cat of Spencer, Iowa.<br/><br/><b>COMMENTS</b><br/>Jawelnofine, I am one of those weirdos who just cannot resist the idea of Dewey the library cat. My whole life w</span>
  <span id="freeText2738992440059717290" style="display:none"><b>BLURB:</b> How much of an impact can an animal have? How many lives can one cat touch? How is it possible for an abandoned kitten to transform a small library, save a classic American town, and eventually become famous around the world? You can't even begin to answer those questions until you hear the charming story of Dewey Readmore Books, the beloved library cat of Spencer, Iowa.<br /><br /><b>COMMENTS</b><br />Jawelnofine, I am one of those weirdos who just cannot resist the idea of Dewey the library cat. My whole life was dedicated to books and cats. It is just one of those things. Then of course, a bonus was the story of the town and the cat. And a town in another country I can learn something about. And the goodness of it all. <i>"Wesley The Owl"</i> by Stacey O'Brien, was another thrill for me. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1173150990">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />Point is, our nuclear little family is animal-crazy. Like you have never seen in your entire life. I will gladly write a book about all our pets, because they were much more than that in our lives. I can sing love songs in their honor, and write endless odes about them. For this reason I have no problem in reading about other people's pets. One of my best childhood reads was <i>Jock Of The Bushveld</i> by Percy FitzPatrick. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/291961.Jock_of_the_Bushveld?ac=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a><br /><br />So yes, this is sooooooo my kind of book. I am in love with Dewey. Period.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_37150788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37150788" />
    <a title="West" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/294699-west"><img alt="West" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1511039381p2/294699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37150788?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="West" href="/user/show/294699-west">West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like reading fluff.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/294699-west?shelf=2008">2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37150788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2479981260890974881">Purely a feel-good story (which can be a good thing or a bad thing, depending on what you like to read). I can't help but feel the author was prone to over-romanticize Dewey and attribute absolute intent all of the time to all of his actions. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong--I am a cat owner/lover myself... But, as a resident realist, the fact that Dewey lived so long, generated so much publicity, and obviously soothed a lonely woman who seemed to have a host of physical (and possibly emotional?) issues may </span>
  <span id="freeText2479981260890974881" style="display:none">Purely a feel-good story (which can be a good thing or a bad thing, depending on what you like to read). I can't help but feel the author was prone to over-romanticize Dewey and attribute absolute intent all of the time to all of his actions. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong--I am a cat owner/lover myself... But, as a resident realist, the fact that Dewey lived so long, generated so much publicity, and obviously soothed a lonely woman who seemed to have a host of physical (and possibly emotional?) issues may have created a greater-than-God cat in the author's mind. <br /><br />Perhaps he was Saint Dewey--and a miracle--for Vicki... But my critical nature keeps me coming back to the fact that we was, in fact, just a cat. He arrived in a library chute on a bitterly frigid January morning. He was a cute and clever cat. And he made many friends along the way "dew" to his pleasant personality. All of these make for a wonderful story. And yes, I cried at the (predictable) ending. But the whole story was told in an almost too-saccharin-y way, for me. Good for a light, heart-warming read, but that's about it.<br /><br />Maybe I would feel differently had I met him in person :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2479981260890974881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Animal lovers and Hallmark commercial cryers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Amanda by: </span>
      GoodReads is advertising it like the second coming
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/645979-amanda?shelf=2008">2008</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer35846556" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18121470662097825505">As I walked out of Penn Station this morning, the proverbial country mouse blinking in the early morning city sunshine, the homesick hole in my heart was filled with a glorious and familiar sight--Borders Bookstore! Oh thank god, finally somewhere I can navigate with familiar ease. And familiarity is an understatement. Every table and shelf looked exactly the same as every table and shelf in the bookstore back home--Cormac McCarthy alongside Love in the Time of Cholera. Jane Green sidling up to </span>
  <span id="freeText18121470662097825505" style="display:none">As I walked out of Penn Station this morning, the proverbial country mouse blinking in the early morning city sunshine, the homesick hole in my heart was filled with a glorious and familiar sight--Borders Bookstore! Oh thank god, finally somewhere I can navigate with familiar ease. And familiarity is an understatement. Every table and shelf looked exactly the same as every table and shelf in the bookstore back home--Cormac McCarthy alongside Love in the Time of Cholera. Jane Green sidling up to Jodi Picoult. And over there, wouldn't you know it? An entire tower dedicated to the Twilight series and associated chachkis. Yep, Borders is ironically unbound by American geography. <br /><br />Except for one thing--Dewey. Dewey doesn't grace our Carolina shelves as abundantly as he does in the Big Apple. This little Iowa pussy has, in fact, made himself quite the cosy home on Seventh Avenue. And I just couldn't resist. Prejudjed as a comely mini-tome for housecoated grannies (regardless of the fact that our own well-respected marketing team has been giving us hairballs for weeks on end), good ol' Dewey is exactly the knitted cardigan type of book you'd expect. The only exception (and not a minor one, in this cat-lover's opinion) is that Dewey the Cat is a fucking awesome, caring, and cuddly kitty. And, true to life, he's not nearly so annoying as the narrator, the library patrons, or the townspeople featured in this quaint feline biography. Granted, I only skimmed this little novel cover to cover, but the cat is heartwarming, even if the humans are conservative lameasses. It was just like being at home... :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18121470662097825505" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2340437244" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340437244" />
    <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda"><img alt="Rachel Aranda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585436207p2/43622386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340437244?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Aranda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Aranda" href="/user/show/43622386-rachel-aranda">Rachel Aranda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/29064436-dewey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=gave-away-or-returned">gave-away-or-returned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340437244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13457169499739015333">This book is a 2.75 rating for me but I'll round to a 3 as I couldn't have finished this book if it wasn't in an audio version. I'd definitely recommend the audio over print.<br/><br/>When I bought this book I thought I was buying a book just about Dewy Readsmore Books, his life at the library, and aspects of how he grew to be the most famous library cat ever. Instead I heard a lot about the private life of his owner, Vicki Myron, and the town both cat and owner call home. This disappointed me as, if I'm </span>
  <span id="freeText13457169499739015333" style="display:none">This book is a 2.75 rating for me but I'll round to a 3 as I couldn't have finished this book if it wasn't in an audio version. I'd definitely recommend the audio over print.<br /><br />When I bought this book I thought I was buying a book just about Dewy Readsmore Books, his life at the library, and aspects of how he grew to be the most famous library cat ever. Instead I heard a lot about the private life of his owner, Vicki Myron, and the town both cat and owner call home. This disappointed me as, if I'm honest I didn't really care about anything not having to do with Dewey. The writing in this book is fine and simple overall. The narrator does a decent job but can be boring at times. There seemed to be a lack of emotion in her voice. I found myself bored with this audiobook and even thought about not finishing it multiple times. If this was the print version I wouldn't have made it as far as I did. This isn't necessarily a bad book but I didn't like it, which surprised me as I usually enjoy stories like this. I just wanted a book about Dewey, not his owner's memoir or his hometown's history. I feel bad for rating this book the way I have but had to be honest in my feelings.<br /><br />Side note: Reading the book along with the audio is how I read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13457169499739015333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37566509?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/1629258-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3733944817810935459">Cats and Books are often a winning combination of mine. Dewey was one of those books that really caught my eye. The story of a small kitten found huddled up one day in a local library in Iowa by a Librarian, cold and close to death.   <span id="freeText3733944817810935459" style="display:none">Cats and Books are often a winning combination of mine. Dewey was one of those books that really caught my eye. The story of a small kitten found huddled up one day in a local library in Iowa by a Librarian, cold and close to death. Named Dewey, his story suddenly spread across not just the USA but all over the world as well, bringing many people together and sharing the love for one furry feline. The passages about Dewey's life as well as the library setting were written well. What let the book down for me, however, were the passages about the history of the town and the life of the author. The pacing then became very slow and I often found myself skipping past to get to the next Dewey scene. An OK read!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/34131006?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace" href="/user/show/177451-grace">Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer34131006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12147621968909013737">This book is certainly a tear-jerker, and one that will appeal to anyone who has a heart, but especially to anyone who works at a library. The book is one of those wonderful experiences where the story may be about a cat, but there are lessons to be learned throughout that can apply to anyone's life. <br/><br/>But the main character is, of course, Dewey himself, who springs to life in such endearing ways. I never tired of hearing about the behavior and antics of this amazing library cat.<br/><br/>My only complaint,</span>
  <span id="freeText12147621968909013737" style="display:none">This book is certainly a tear-jerker, and one that will appeal to anyone who has a heart, but especially to anyone who works at a library. The book is one of those wonderful experiences where the story may be about a cat, but there are lessons to be learned throughout that can apply to anyone's life. <br /><br />But the main character is, of course, Dewey himself, who springs to life in such endearing ways. I never tired of hearing about the behavior and antics of this amazing library cat.<br /><br />My only complaint, and the only thing that makes this 4 and not 5 stars, was that the writing style was frustrating in spots. Specifically, the person transcribing what Vicki said seemed to plan to return to certain topics, and then never did. There were several points at which the phrasing led you to believe that something would happen and it didn't. Things like (this isn't in the book, just an example of the sort of thing I mean) "Little did I know that this would just be the beginning..." followed by no elaboration on the topic. At first it was just a little distracting, but by the end it got annoying. The flow just seemed a bit random.<br /><br />But what the book lacked in cohesiveness, it made up for in heart, definitely.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12147621968909013737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_282707620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/282707620" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6257531-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329765864p2/6257531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/282707620?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/6257531-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6257531-caroline?shelf=animals">animals</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6257531-caroline?shelf=bedtime-reading">bedtime-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer282707620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14124039247443515508">I’m a lark. At 5.00am in the morning I can read anything. In fact I’m up for a challenge. But as the day wears on I flag. Come 11pm at night my brain is mush, and my bedtime reading has to be easy, soothing and happy. Stodge for the eyes. It has to go down like my favourite pudding.<br/><br/><i>“Dewey – The small-town library-cat who touched the world”</i> was in this vein. It should have appealed to bedtime me – I am completely besotted with cats, and with libraries for that matter..... but it didn’t. The book </span>
  <span id="freeText14124039247443515508" style="display:none">I’m a lark. At 5.00am in the morning I can read anything. In fact I’m up for a challenge. But as the day wears on I flag. Come 11pm at night my brain is mush, and my bedtime reading has to be easy, soothing and happy. Stodge for the eyes. It has to go down like my favourite pudding.<br /><br /><i>“Dewey – The small-town library-cat who touched the world”</i> was in this vein. It should have appealed to bedtime me – I am completely besotted with cats, and with libraries for that matter..... but it didn’t. The book was deeply earnest in tone. There were two dissonant threads, firstly, a story about a wonderful cat, and secondly, the story of the sad life (blighted by various tragedies), of the woman who ran the library, and looked after Dewey. This librarian was fantastically brave throughout all her negative experiences, but they pealed like a gong throughout the book. For me her distresses detracted from Dewey’s story. (I know that's an awful thing to say, but they did....)<br /><br />I was also let down in that Dewey the cat didn’t really come alive for me. There were several occasions where I could have found myself dabbing my eyes with tissues and aww-ing at Dewey’s adorableness, but this didn’t happen. Instead we were given lots of statistics to prove his lovability (e.g. when people were asked to choose a name for him, hundreds responded, and when he died the librarian received more than a thousand emails conveying sympathy), but this was proof from the outside. I wanted proof in my heart, and it never happened. I never experienced Dewey’s wonderfulness for myself. Judging by the statistics, and descriptions of Dewey’s behaviour, he really was a very exceptional cat, loved by many people…but I never really felt it for myself.<br /><br />I feel a mean and horrible person for not liking this book more. 25,689 people have rated it here at Goodreads (now that is a phenomenal number of people!) with an average rating of 3.77.... but it just didn’t turn me on.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14124039247443515508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1542355715" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1542355715" />
    <a title="Rikke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke"><img alt="Rikke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594580741p2/4327582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1542355715?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rikke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rikke" href="/user/show/4327582-rikke">Rikke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=books-about-cats">books-about-cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542355715" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18161934820596507585">I love cats. I love libraries. But God, I loathed this.<br/><br/>Not because of Dewey, of course. Dewey seems like the sweetest kitten that ever graced earth – like most kittens do. He lived in a library and made the life of the librarians a bit sweeter and lovelier just by being there. He was rescued, and he rescued others in turn. He made a difference just by existing. As pets often do. <br/><br/>The parts of this book concerning Dewey's routines and habits were overly cute. I adored reading about Dewey's quest f</span>
  <span id="freeText18161934820596507585" style="display:none">I love cats. I love libraries. But God, I loathed this.<br /><br />Not because of Dewey, of course. Dewey seems like the sweetest kitten that ever graced earth – like most kittens do. He lived in a library and made the life of the librarians a bit sweeter and lovelier just by being there. He was rescued, and he rescued others in turn. He made a difference just by existing. As pets often do. <br /><br />The parts of this book concerning Dewey's routines and habits were overly cute. I adored reading about Dewey's quest for rubber bands and his ability to locate and to fall asleep in every open drawer, cupboard or empty box he could find. Cats are cute. And Dewey is no exception to this rule. <br /><br />But, the way this book is written is tedious. Myron constantly tells the reader that <i>she</i> knows, what Dewey is thinking. And not in a fun, trying-to-figure-out-what-the-cat-is-thinking-way. No. In a obnoxious, overbearing and much too selfreasurring way. An example: “<i>He regarded it as his job to make the library a place where people could be happy</i>”. Myron forcer her own sense of higher purpose on a cat in order to give him a noble cause. But who says that Dewey didn't regard it as his job to purr and to sleep all day?<br /><br />At other times, the book reads as written by an 8-year old. Myron observes how Dewey is around everyone else and smugly notes, that they think <i>they</i> have a special relationsship with Dewey even though he treats everyone the same. Her point is that Dewey is generally good and loves everyone equally, and she laughs at those endearingly naive people thinking that they are something special. But of course, Myron reaffirms, her <i>own</i> relationsship with Dewey <i>is</i> special. Dewey loves her the most, and while that may be true (she does serve him his food, after all), it is tedious to read about. I felt like part of the story was narrated by a jealous little child.<br /><br />This book is also interwoven with personal anecdotes from Myron's own life as well as long tirades on Iowa's economy and beautiful landscapes. Not only was it pointless to read, it was also painfully bad written. And worst of all, I didn't care. I only wanted the cute cat anecdotes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18161934820596507585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780446555418" href="/book/show/12126178-dewey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43622386-rachel-aranda?shelf=library-rentals">library-rentals</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819782614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12954260180402227153">When I bought this book I thought I was buying a book just about Dewy Readsmore Books, his life at the library, and aspects of how he grew to be the most famous library cat ever. Instead I heard a lot about the private life of his owner, Vicki Myron, and the town both cat and owner call home. This disappointed me as, if I'm honest I didn't really care about anything not having to do with Dewey. The writing in this book is fine and simple overall. The narrator does a decent job but can be boring </span>
  <span id="freeText12954260180402227153" style="display:none">When I bought this book I thought I was buying a book just about Dewy Readsmore Books, his life at the library, and aspects of how he grew to be the most famous library cat ever. Instead I heard a lot about the private life of his owner, Vicki Myron, and the town both cat and owner call home. This disappointed me as, if I'm honest I didn't really care about anything not having to do with Dewey. The writing in this book is fine and simple overall. The narrator does a decent job but can be boring at times. There seemed to be a lack of emotion in her voice. I found myself bored with this audiobook and even thought about not finishing it multiple times. If this was the print version I wouldn't have made it as far as I did. This isn't necessarily a bad book but I didn't like it, which surprised me as I usually enjoy stories like this. I just wanted a book about Dewey, not his owner's memoir or his hometown's history. I feel bad for rating this book the way I have but had to be honest in my feelings; this book is a 2.75 rating for me. I'd definitely recommend the audio over print. <br /><br />Side note: Reading the book along with the audio is how I read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12954260180402227153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100562749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7381258063495574161">This book is as much about Spencer, Iowa and the people who live there as it is about Dewey the cat. The author (a librarian in Spencer) tells of the people in the town and how Dewey affected their lives for the better. She chronicles his life from when he came to the library as an abandoned kitten to his death at age 19. While heartwarming, this isn't a cutsie story about a kitty cat. The town, the librarian, and the cat are all survivors of hard times. An enjoyable read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2823640629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2823640629" />
    <a title="Skip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1389748-skip"><img alt="Skip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231161516p2/1389748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2823640629?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skip" href="/user/show/1389748-skip">Skip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8141643-dewey">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=biography-memoirs">biography-memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2823640629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16794487082218607873">If you love cats or libraries or both, this book is for you. I do. A small gray kitten is found in a book slot deposit, more dead than alive, in the middle of an Iowan winter. After a bath, a warm-up, and a recovery from frostbitten feet pads, it turns out the kitten is an orange tabby; he is adopted by the Spencer Free Library and after a naming contest, becomes Dewey Readmore Books. In the 1980s, things were rough in Iowa: farmers went bankrupt, then their banks followed, and towns too. Dewey,</span>
  <span id="freeText16794487082218607873" style="display:none">If you love cats or libraries or both, this book is for you. I do. A small gray kitten is found in a book slot deposit, more dead than alive, in the middle of an Iowan winter. After a bath, a warm-up, and a recovery from frostbitten feet pads, it turns out the kitten is an orange tabby; he is adopted by the Spencer Free Library and after a naming contest, becomes Dewey Readmore Books. In the 1980s, things were rough in Iowa: farmers went bankrupt, then their banks followed, and towns too. Dewey, on the other hand, seemed to represent hope: he had a knack for making friends, seeming to intuitively know who needed his help most, such as the head librarian (serious health problems) or handicapped children or someone having a bad day. His antics are very funny for cat lovers, such as his love for catnip, rubber bands, boxes, etc. There is a great story about his trying to alert the staff to a bat loose in the library. Dewey's fame spread everywhere because he was special.<br /><br />P.S. My only complaint was that like <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> movie, it ended too many times.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16794487082218607873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40882480" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40882480" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40882480?book_show_action=true">Dec 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=midwest">midwest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40882480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10269033970316137534">This book has irritated and disappointed me so much that I'm taking a few minutes to bash it.<br/><br/>I first saw "Dewey" in a book store before Christmas. I read the first page of the introduction while standing in front of the new books display, and I loved it. That first page was one of the best descriptions of Iowa I've read -- it perfectly summarized how I feel about my home state.<br/><br/>"There is a thousand mile table of land in the middle of the United States, between the Mississippi River on the East an</span>
  <span id="freeText10269033970316137534" style="display:none">This book has irritated and disappointed me so much that I'm taking a few minutes to bash it.<br /><br />I first saw "Dewey" in a book store before Christmas. I read the first page of the introduction while standing in front of the new books display, and I loved it. That first page was one of the best descriptions of Iowa I've read -- it perfectly summarized how I feel about my home state.<br /><br />"There is a thousand mile table of land in the middle of the United States, between the Mississippi River on the East and the deserts on the West. Out here, there are rolling hills, but no mountains. There are rivers and creeks, but few large lakes. The wind has worn down the rock outcroppings, turning them first to dust, then dirt, then soil, and finally to fine black farmland. Out here, the roads are straight, stretching to the horizon in long, unbroken lines. There are no corners, only occasional, almost imperceptible bends. This land was surveyed and plotted for farms; the bends are corrections in the survey line. Exactly every mile, every road is intersected by another almost perfectly straight road. Inside is a square mile of farmland. Take a million of those square miles, lace them together, and you have one of the most important agricultural regions in the world. The Great Plains. The Bread Basket. The Heartland. Or as many people think of it, the place you fly over on your way to somewhere else. Let them have the oceans and mountains, their beaches and their ski resorts. I’ll take Iowa."<br /><br />Great paragraph, right? Well, enjoy it, because it's the last great graph in the book.<br /><br />So, I finally get the book from the library, and I'm happy to read about this cat that got abandoned in a library book slot in a small Iowa town. By this time, the book is a full-fledged bestseller, so I'm optimistic.<br /><br />Sadly, the book quickly degenerates into a recount of every cute thing the damn cat ever did. Remember the time Dewey chewed on some rubber bands? Or how about the time he crawled into the lap of a Grumpy Old Man and made him smile? Gee whiz, that cat sure is cute!<br /><br />Gag, and gag again. I read about 30 pages, and then I started skimming, hoping it would improve. Soon, I couldn't even handle skimming the stories, because the writing style was so childish and grating. This book seems to be written for an 8-year-old girl who loves cats, but it mistakenly got put on the Adult Nonfiction shelf.<br /><br />I will grant that there is a good two-page explanation on the Farm Crisis of the 1980s, and how it devastated so many Iowa families. The writer thinks the farm crisis boosted Dewey's popularity in the town, because he cheered up so many people during a tough time.<br /><br />That may be true, but there doesn't need to be 288 pages on how cute this one library cat was. <br /><br />And I'm sure that one of the reasons this book is so popular now is because there is another financial crisis, and people apparently want sentimental pap to cheer them up. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10269033970316137534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+D4WmcPZ+KWHcMtUf4nRh1OBueV7Ti5hasxe3uDqD08ucfxQUQ8FPZJCBtQgs5S8ICz7DH5GNjjpDFnRDdv2Nw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WGWgyOAaau46KcSnQpRFlOQZwSnxi5zhKStViVYSXESOKkoBcsyXdi8bCScdrgCvl7SDwPSDhLiq61KGuyOlPA==')})
  }
